  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_db2a9fe7-816d-4836-b1fc-9af447f155ca'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/714852-for-those-who-have-read-it-what-age">For those who have read it, what age bracket would you put it at? YA? Adult? I know this author has written for adults before, but the description leaves me curious.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_714852'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28204534-paper-girls-vol-1">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/19285370-doug-goodman"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1473680380i/19285370._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/19285370-doug-goodman">Doug Goodman</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Vol 1 works as an older YA. There is some horror imagery, a kid who smokes, some cussing - the kinds of things that some parents may feel a bit leery <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Vol 1 works as an older YA. There is some horror imagery, a kid who smokes, some cussing - the kinds of things that some parents may feel a bit leery of letting their twelve year old read. I would recommend ages 13-15 depending on how comfortable you are with the text.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1303981-anyone-know-what-the-bad-guys-are-saying">anyone know what the bad guys are saying? is it a real language or fictional?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1303981'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28204534-paper-girls-vol-1">like</a></span>

</li>

</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/20954866-travis"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/20954866-travis">Travis</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If you are referring to the language spoken by the mutant-looking characters, it is English written in an invented script. The second volume includes <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If you are referring to the language spoken by the mutant-looking characters, it is English written in an invented script. The second volume includes a section that shows both the script and the plain English equivalent and that is a point you can use to get started deciphering it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1728999343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1728999343" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728999343?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=youre-a-graphic-novel">youre-a-graphic-novel</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728999343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6293010694680003576"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best graphic novels & comics category 2016!</b><br/><br/>three stars with room to grow.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5569_zpsdtungjey.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072407._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo IMG_5569_zpsdtungjey.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>while impatiently waiting for more installments of saga to come out, i decided to check out this other brian k. vaughan book, because i liked the cover, the synopsis promised me plucky girls, 80's references, and this right here is how you get my attention:<br/><br/><i>Suburban drama and supernatural mysteries collide in this smash-hit series about nostalgia, first jobs, and the last days </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6293010694680003576" style="display:none"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best graphic novels &amp; comics category 2016!</b><br><br>three stars with room to grow.<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5569_zpsdtungjey.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072407._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5569_zpsdtungjey.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>while impatiently waiting for more installments of saga to come out, i decided to check out this other brian k. vaughan book, because i liked the cover, the synopsis promised me plucky girls, 80's references, and this right here is how you get my attention:<br><br><i>Suburban drama and supernatural mysteries collide in this smash-hit series about nostalgia, first jobs, and the last days of childhood.</i><br><br>all my sweet spots = accounted for. <br><br>because, yes - plucky girls:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5565_zpsqgdtxqy6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072410._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5565_zpsqgdtxqy6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>80's references:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5566_zpsu0umdqbn.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072409._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5566_zpsu0umdqbn.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>nostalgia (for me, anyway - this picture made my heart soften):<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5567_zpskl8xscrc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072408._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5567_zpskl8xscrc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and there are also some pretty funny 80's-flavored dream sequences:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5571_zpsy7ogbzqw.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072406._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5571_zpsy7ogbzqw.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>i'm just not hooked yet. it's no saga, that's for sure. but in a more positive light, it's actually what i thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22554204.Lumberjanes__Vol__1_Beware_the_Kitten_Holy" title="Lumberjanes, Vol. 1 Beware the Kitten Holy by Noelle Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumberjanes, Vol. 1: Beware the Kitten Holy</a> was going to be, before realizing that series was for a much younger reading age. this one has all the girl-power and female bonding and general badassery-adventure setup as <i>Lumberjanes</i>, but with significantly more guns, cussin' and good-natured pal-ribbin', pterodactyls, and actual danger, and it is far less p.c. because it was the 80's, my friends, and twelve-year-old internetless kids from the suburbs didn't always have access to the rich spectrum of life and they sometimes said "faggot." but if time travelers can forgive a kid for their squeamishness:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5572_zpsk4mt6fvk.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072405._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5572_zpsk4mt6fvk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>so can we. and for being set in midwestern 80's suburbia, there's some decent diversity in the characters here - there's a jewish girl and a vietnamese(?) girl and an adopted girl of indeterminate race and everyone's favorite stereotype: a chain-smoking irish-american lass, tough and redheaded and on her way to becoming a criminal just like the rest of her family! but apart from her homophobia and the cliché of her, she's pretty rad - willing to step up and throw down for her equally-fierce pack of paper girls against the most unexpected foes.<br><br>i didn't always understand what was going on, but i'm confident it will all become clearer in future volumes. i'm intrigued enough to continue with the series - i'm not in love with it, but it's got potential and i'll check back in next volume to see if it's getting there yet, if only to enjoy more 80's background details.<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/flat%20stanley001/IMG_5564_zpskuvqfkox.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471555248i/20072411._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_5564_zpskuvqfkox.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_2073016286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073016286" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073016286?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The Female Dr Who</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073016286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9410727519230765790">Heh. I'm a full-on idiot. <br/>I (<i>because reading the blurb is for losers!</i>) thought that the title was some kind of catchy metaphorical shit. Like, they were <i>girls</i> whose young emotions were as thin as <i>paper</i>. Or instead of <i>paper dolls</i> they were <i>paper girls</i>. You know, something along those lines.<br/>For some reason, it never occurred to me that this was about a bunch of girls with a paper route. Probably because that one chick on the cover has a cigg dangling from her lips, making me think they were a tad </span>
  <span id="freeText9410727519230765790" style="display:none">Heh. I'm a full-on idiot. <br>I (<i>because reading the blurb is for losers!</i>) thought that the title was some kind of catchy metaphorical shit. Like, they were <i>girls</i> whose young emotions were as thin as <i>paper</i>. Or instead of <i>paper dolls</i> they were <i>paper girls</i>. You know, something along those lines.<br>For some reason, it never occurred to me that this was about a bunch of girls with a paper route. Probably because that one chick on the cover has a cigg dangling from her lips, making me think they were a tad older than your average kid on a bike tossing the Times at your porch. But since we all knew that kid in middle school who was a little more 'advanced' than the rest of us, I should've known better. My bad.<br><b>So. They're <i>actual</i> Paper Girls.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502109750i/23525187._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>And now that <i>that's</i> out of the way, I feel I should tell you that this story doesn't have <i>anything</i> to do with their respective paper routes.<br>Nope. This is all about interdimensional time travel.<br><b>Whoo-hoo!</b><br>Or not...depending on how you feel about a middle school version of Dr. Who.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502109750i/23525188._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This seems to be a hit or miss title with my friends, and from what I can tell, it looks like most of the complaints center around all the sci-fi <i>whatthefuckery</i> that happens with little to no explanation. Plus, you've gotta translate some of what this one person says. I mean, the other guys sound normal, but the crazy chick that's hunting them down for unknown reasons?<br><b>Wez timetravlrs! Goona kilz yu!</b><i> &lt;--not a real quote, btw</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502109750i/23525189._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Without any real reference point for some of this stuff, I can see how this volume might come across as too wonky and out there to enjoy. So, for those of you who didn't care for this, I can totally see where you're coming from.<br><b>But.</b><br>And here's where being a full-on idiot comes in handy: I accidentally read the 2nd volume first, so I knew where everything was headed.<br><i><b>Ta-da!</b><br>Can't nobody tell me being a moron don't have its advantages...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502112411ra/23525568.gif" width="375" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, you see the <i>tiny</i> little 1 &amp; 2 underneath the title on those two covers in the image below? Well, I didn't. I had both of them sitting on my kitchen table and just grabbed the one I <i>thought</i> was the 1st volume and headed out to the park with my girls. And while they ran around getting wet in the splash pad and falling off of the top of the playground equipment, I read a very interesting graphic novel. I mean, sure I thought it was odd that I was kinda plopped down into the middle of a story, but I assumed there would be a flashback at some point to explain. Turns out there <i>was</i> a flashback sequence...it was called <b>Paper Girls: volume 1</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502110355i/23525297._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>What I'm <i>trying</i> to say is that I had a distinct advantage going into this. I already knew what some of the (seemingly) nonsense stuff was leading towards, so it didn't have me scratching my head the way it did some of my friends. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502111765i/23525449._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Even so, this volume didn't blow my mind. I liked all the 80's references and the timey-wimey stuff, but Cliff Chang's art isn't really my jam. <br><i>*whispers* <br>Please don't hurt me...please don't hurt me...please don't hurt me...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502112638ra/23525593.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>He's super-talented &amp; I know a lot of you love his style, so don't think that I'm trying to put him down as an artist. I'm not. And it doesn't make my eyes bleed to look at it or anything, but it's not something that makes me <i>personally</i> want to keep turning the pages just to look at the pictures.<br>However, since I've already read (and liked!) volume 2, I'm pretty invested in some of these characters and I'd like to see where this story takes them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9410727519230765790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1576800173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576800173" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576800173?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-superhero-scifi-fantasy">gn-superhero-scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-ya">gn-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576800173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7140743887132747315">Update, 6/19/18: Once again, re-reading for my YA GN and Comics class with a focus on kick-ass girls. In this case, 4 of them, 12 years old, who are delivering papers in the Cleveland suburb of Stony Stream on All Saints Day (the day after Halloween) when revelers in costumes can still be seen roaming the streets. . . among aliens in costumes. And pterodactyls. And monsters. And time travel so you can meet your future self. Too crazy, some Goodreads reviewers said, I don't know what the hell is </span>
  <span id="freeText7140743887132747315" style="display:none">Update, 6/19/18: Once again, re-reading for my YA GN and Comics class with a focus on kick-ass girls. In this case, 4 of them, 12 years old, who are delivering papers in the Cleveland suburb of Stony Stream on All Saints Day (the day after Halloween) when revelers in costumes can still be seen roaming the streets. . . among aliens in costumes. And pterodactyls. And monsters. And time travel so you can meet your future self. Too crazy, some Goodreads reviewers said, I don't know what the hell is going on! I say keep reading, relax, have fun. This is a madcap and heartfelt homage to all things eighties, especially films such as ET and Peggy Sue Gets Married and Back to the Future. My fourth reading, and now that I see what is coming, I like it even more! As with any good book, most of what is coming in later volumes is right there in the beginning. But you don't know it first read, so relax!<br /><br />Update, June, 2017: I reread this once again for my summer class on YA comics with a focus on girls. Having read the existing subsequent volumes, I like this crazy first volume even more than I originally did! <br /><br />June, 2016: I just read this for the first time in March 2016, and reread it again for my summer YA GN class. One woman in class said she liked it better than Ms. Marvel, Vol. 1, (G. Willow Wilson version) because the girls in this story swore more. :) Oh, they all swear in Vaughn comics, I said; if that's your standard of success, read all the Vaughn! But they do feel a bit more "real" for that, I suppose. The comic is edgier than Ms. Marvel (Kamala Khan), in some ways: Kamala is more wholesome and idealistic than the girls in Paper Girls, but why choose, read them both, they are both fun. I liked reading it through better a second time, but I still want to know more about what is going on. I will eagerly read on as next issues comes out soon.<br /><br />Initial review, 3/16: I had read the floppies for much of this first volume, but was excited to read it all in one sitting. Vaughn is a terrific writer of dialogue, clever, smart-ass, and he loves to have at least a couple (slightly) foul-mouthed characters in the mix, and sure, they sound like a lot of other Vaughn characters, but who cares, he is one of the best ever. The feel of it is great. The art by Chiang is awesome, capturing the eighties vibe. Vaughn all the way through peppers his text with fun eighties references (and I am not an eighties guy, I'm a sixties and seventies guy, but I appreciate the effort). The neon colors are wonderful, by Matt Wilson. You can see it, right, in the cover? Since it largely takes place at night it is a little darker, of course, but still amazing, award-worthy YA coloring.<br /><br />It's a YA text (though some schools/libraries may have trouble with some of the bad language, but Vaughn doesn't probably necessarily think of comics as something to be read IN school, at least not this one), featuring four Cleveland (Vaughn is from Cleveland) twelve year old Paper Girls (younguns, they actually deliver papers in the wee hours of the morn, as I once did at that age, as most papers were delivered in those days, though in my day girls didn't deliver, sfatey issues were named as the reason, so in that sense the story is a cool fantasy). They fit very well with Kamala Kahn (Ms Marvel) and other wonderful new kick-ass girl comics in this amazing time for that. The girls are not at first read for me very distinct yet, there is very little actual character development, as this is the all out action first issue, so I expect we will slow down in volume 2 and get to know the girls a bit more.<br /><br />The action is ET (with kids on bicycles riding in the night at high speed, only all girls) meets Stand By Me (only, again, all girls), and this is for an older guy not SO interesting as a plot, yet. A little too crazy, a little too much, feels a little breathless on first read. And shades of Buffy, too, in all the best ways. Brian and Joss Whedon must have a grand old time socially. A new century Algonqiuin Round Table (look it up kids: Dorothy Parker, Robert Benchley, Alexander Woolcott, George S. Kauffman), with all the crackling wit.<br /><br />Anyway, the action. A lot happens and very little happens on this night of all nights; it's all flash in the pan--so far. The girls proceed on this Halloween night of 1988 and meet three boys who are just sexist creeps, one of them in a Freddy Krueger costume, though more bark than bite, really. Sets up the "real" All Saints Day scare. Three ninjas. Then three aliens. Four against three, balance against imbalance. And pterodactyls. And time travel, ala Back to the Future, sort of. And the eighties refs have to keep a comin', Mask, walkie talkies instead of cell phones. And in the middle of the apocalypse, one of them says, "wait, you guys give out whole candy bars for Halloween!? What's up with that?" :) Steve Jobs and Apple come in here, though at this point it is Apple meets eighties walkie talkies.<br /><br />And for the YA crowd, the action has to be over the top, but you know, it's Halloween, it has to be breathless, running through the night--is it an actual werewolf or a werewolf costume?--with everything but the kitchen sink thrown at them. But no eek screaming girly stuff, they are tough and resourceful, of course, this is 2016 comics! Girls rule!<br /><br />This is my reason for four instead of five stars, or one of them, that all this pizzazz is happening, and we have no idea what is happening, and we don't really yet know much about the girls, it is all sort of whizzbang superficial in the early going. But if I were inclined to give it three stars (you have at least that for the dialogue and Chiang and color, c'mon!), I have to give it one extra star just because I know the intended audiences--1) younger folks, teens and 2) eighties folks who lived through 1988--will love it. I liked it a lot for what it is and forgive it for what it is not yet. I totally trust Vaughn to make you feel deeply and laugh a lot and resolve this with some reference to politics and human nature in satisfying plot resolution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7140743887132747315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1704929365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169215145979722584">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Boy, this one had <b>A LOT</b> of stuff going on. Luckily for Erin, the other paper girls have already hit the streets and appear just in time to save the day. Not so lucky is the first impression pres</span>
  <span id="freeText12169215145979722584" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Boy, this one had <b>A LOT</b> of stuff going on. Buckle up, kids, and I’ll <s>take you on a crazy acid trip</s> explain things . . . sort of.<br><br>Our story begins in the wee hours of Halloween when noob Erin is being accosted by local hooligan Freddie Krueger while attempting to complete her paper route. Luckily for Erin, the other paper girls have already hit the streets and appear just in time to save the day. Not so lucky is the first impression presented . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469113918i/19781926._SY540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Uh. Yeah. <br><br>So anyfarts, the girls make their escape and immediately run into another problem when they make plans to divide and conquer the paper delivery. While attempting to get payback on the thugs responsible, they instead find something they <b>really</b> weren’t expecting . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469113918i/19781927._SX540_.png" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Once again they narrowly get away and finally come face to face with the potential bad guys who look an awful lot like this fella when their masks are removed . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469113918ra/19781928.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>We then discover the key to solving the entire WTFery that has been going on might be in a tiny little device with the logo of a bitten apple on it . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469113918ra/19781929.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But wait, that’s not all. No, there are <b>DINOSAURS</b> added to the mix next. Y’all know there’s only room in my heart for one dinosaur story . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469114105ra/19781962.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(Thank you to EVERYONE who has sent me this gif. I finally had a chance to use it.)<br><br>There’s also aliens who speak some form of hipsterish Shakespearean throwback/fastforward language that had me all . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469113918ra/19781931.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As well as another dude who bore a striking resemblance to . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469113918ra/19781932.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Not to mention the bizarre dream sequences starring folks like The Gipper . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469113918i/19781933._SX540_.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Since I’m stupid it took me awhile to figure out this was a Throwback Thursday selection. I thought Mac was just a homophobic asshole with her remarks (and she was), but supposedly it was the language of the time (and sadly it was) so it was used in that one frame. Eventually with various Dukakis references and a shout-out to one of my all-time faves . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469113918ra/19781934.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was able to put two and two together. It still didn’t make this any less of a hot mess, however. I debated giving this 2 Stars but this is the dude who wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242003939?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Saga</a> FFS. There's no excuse for this one.<br><br><i>ARC provided by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you, NetGalley!</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12169215145979722584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=image">image</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=youth">youth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32295170-jan-philipzig?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1682105742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5136997132170501063">LOVED the first issue (no surprise there, first issues are a Vaughan specialty), the late 80s setting, Chiang's clean and subtle artwork, Wilson's neon-drenched coloring, the lively, primarily female cast, the snappy yet realistic dialogue – loved it all so much I got a little dizzy early on. Then came the disfigured teenagers from the future, the dinosaurs, the weird language, the Apple dude - and I got a bit confused. Which was the idea, I guess. Not yet sure how it’ll all come together, hope </span>
  <span id="freeText5136997132170501063" style="display:none">LOVED the first issue (no surprise there, first issues are a Vaughan specialty), the late 80s setting, Chiang's clean and subtle artwork, Wilson's neon-drenched coloring, the lively, primarily female cast, the snappy yet realistic dialogue – loved it all so much I got a little dizzy early on. Then came the disfigured teenagers from the future, the dinosaurs, the weird language, the Apple dude - and I got a bit confused. Which was the idea, I guess. Not yet sure how it’ll all come together, hope the time-travel angle won’t overwhelm what I love most about the story so far: its young protagonists.<br /><br />It's a charming and very enjoyable first volume that brings to mind Brubaker's <i>Deadenders</i> and movies like <i>Stand by Me</i>, <i>E.T.</i> and <i>Looper</i>, but adds a feminist edge. I’m definitely on board for more!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9744794489514114468">While waiting for the next Saga volume to come out I thought to check out another series from Brian K. Vaughan. I enjoyed it but I don't think it is as good as the other. It was weird with different strange creatures and an attractive 80' vibe. I might continue with the series but i am in no rush to do so. </span>

        <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal">Saania Zee Jamal ϟ</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735203612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14914078760700218749"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460357881i/18729189._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>LOOK AT THAT BEAUTY. <br/>SO PLEASING, SO PROMISING.<br/><br/>But agh.<br/><br/>Mr. Vaughan, I'm afraid you've set the bar way too high after <i>Saga.</i> While <i>Paper Girls</i> certainly stands out in the world of comics, with a vibrant spectacle of <b>colours</b> and <b>rich atmosphere</b>, it definitely isn't the best this man's got to offer.<br/><br/>Other than lack of a smooth-running plot, this story's fallout lay in its <b>dialogue</b> for me. And by that I mean the fact that nearly 20% of it is either in a language we don't understand or some really bad </span>
  <span id="freeText14914078760700218749" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460357881i/18729189._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>LOOK AT THAT BEAUTY. <br>SO PLEASING, SO PROMISING.<br><br>But agh.<br><br>Mr. Vaughan, I'm afraid you've set the bar way too high after <i>Saga.</i> While <i>Paper Girls</i> certainly stands out in the world of comics, with a vibrant spectacle of <b>colours</b> and <b>rich atmosphere</b>, it definitely isn't the best this man's got to offer.<br><br>Other than lack of a smooth-running plot, this story's fallout lay in its <b>dialogue</b> for me. And by that I mean the fact that nearly 20% of it is either in a language we don't understand or some really bad ghetto Shakespeare. I'm sure there's a translation lurking about in the interwebs somewhere but it only serves to be supremely off-putting when you're lost reading in the middle it.<br><br>Back to the <b>roughly handled plotline</b>. The story? Great. Not mind-blowing, not whoa-inducing, but still great. It manages to capture the quick paced, compact structure every comic books needs to win an audience, but not without its stumbles along the way. Too much infodump in too little time and what we're left with is confuddling <b>chaos.</b><br><br>As for the characters? <b>Meh.</b> That's all they made me feel and that's all I've got to say about them. Sure, there were two or three interesting turn of events thrown at us and some insanely <b><i>lush</i> artwork</b> to boot too (big hats off to Cliff Chiang and Matthew Wilson!) But in the end, these girls and this world seem just as flat as paper.<br><br><u>Final rating: 2.75 stars.</u><br><br>P.S. I'm still trying to figure out what the symbolism with all the apples and eyes is about...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483389238i/21607677._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="224" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>_____________________________<br><br><b>Book song: Ain't No Rest For The Wicked by Cage The Elephant</b><br>_____________________________</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2173430160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14616400749318423881">TW: homophobia (+ usage of word f****t), suicide attempt<br/><br/>This book was just so genius. The best way I can describe it is Saga meets Stranger Things. I loved the concept of a girl squad running around to solve the world's issues. I loved the sass, the artwork, the clothing and the vibe of the entire book. I love each girl in the group for their own reasons, and I didn't find myself thinking, "wait, who is this person?" like I usually do in graphic novels. As far as a feminist graphic novel, I enjo</span>
  <span id="freeText14616400749318423881" style="display:none">TW: homophobia (+ usage of word f****t), suicide attempt<br /><br />This book was just so genius. The best way I can describe it is Saga meets Stranger Things. I loved the concept of a girl squad running around to solve the world's issues. I loved the sass, the artwork, the clothing and the vibe of the entire book. I love each girl in the group for their own reasons, and I didn't find myself thinking, "wait, who is this person?" like I usually do in graphic novels. As far as a feminist graphic novel, I enjoyed this one more than Bitch Planet, which was weighted down with a lot of boring and aimless dialogue whereas I was glued onto every page of this. Because this book deals with time travel, it was so cool to see pop culture references from both our time and the 80s. <br /><br />A lot of people say that the plot of this is confusing, but compared to the mindfuck that is the Saga series, I actually followed it alright. It leaves you with unanswered questions, but those should definitely (and hopefully) be resolved in later volumes which I plan to pick up.<br /><br />There was a character who would make homophobic remarks, but they always went challenged by other characters. I can't wait for (and hope to see) the development and growth of this character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14616400749318423881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4399789059826958312"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>So... not amazing, unfortunately. In fact the only thing I <i>super</i> loved about this was the illustrations. <br/><br/>It's a little difficult for me not to compare this to Vaughn's other ongoing series <i>Saga,</i> which had me hooked from the very first installment. <br/><br/><b>This was was very <u>okay.</u></b><br/><br/>Vol. 1 could've benefitted from being a bit longer, providing a little more depth of plot and characterization. <br/><br/>I was really feeling a young, diverse female cast on an 80's science fiction adventure. I was</span>
  <span id="freeText4399789059826958312" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />So... not amazing, unfortunately. In fact the only thing I <i>super</i> loved about this was the illustrations. <br /><br />It's a little difficult for me not to compare this to Vaughn's other ongoing series <i>Saga,</i> which had me hooked from the very first installment. <br /><br /><b>This was was very <u>okay.</u></b><br /><br />Vol. 1 could've benefitted from being a bit longer, providing a little more depth of plot and characterization. <br /><br />I was really feeling a young, diverse female cast on an 80's science fiction adventure. I was even getting a <i>Stranger Things</i> vibe from it at the beginning. <br /><br />But alas, there just isn't a lot of <b>substance</b> here.<br /><br />I'll likely try out Vol. 2 before writing the series off to see if it gets its footing, but a <u>disappointing</u> introduction to say the least.</span>

<div id="review_1984370836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984370836" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984370836?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=hugo-2017">hugo-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-man">author-man</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984370836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16646905071999296967">4ish stars.<br/><br/>A cool first volume, not at all what I expected, but in a good way. The plot is honestly kind of wacky. Weird dinosaurs and time/space travelers, maybe? I honestly didn't know what was going on like 60% of the time, but strangely it didn't bug me... There's a Stranger Things vibe with the 80s setting and the kid protagonists. <br/><br/>The Paper Girls themselves are awfully mature for their what- 12ish years? I had a hard time buying their ages. Maybe I'm just out of touch with the young 'uns t</span>
  <span id="freeText16646905071999296967" style="display:none">4ish stars.<br /><br />A cool first volume, not at all what I expected, but in a good way. The plot is honestly kind of wacky. Weird dinosaurs and time/space travelers, maybe? I honestly didn't know what was going on like 60% of the time, but strangely it didn't bug me... There's a Stranger Things vibe with the 80s setting and the kid protagonists. <br /><br />The Paper Girls themselves are awfully mature for their what- 12ish years? I had a hard time buying their ages. Maybe I'm just out of touch with the young 'uns these days. I did like all of them, though, especially Erin, and I like each of their artistic representations. I feel like, characteristically, they'll grow and deepen as the series continues.<br /><br />I really like Chiang's art. It isn't mind-blowingly gorgeous or incredibly detailed and it's unfair to compare it to that of Fiona Staples who does the art for Vaughan's other incredibly popular series, Saga. But it does a great job telling the story. It's consistent throughout which, despite what one might think, is pretty rare in most graphic novels. I never became confused by the art and for that, I think it's great. Matt Wilson, the colorist, does a spectacular job, particularly with gradiating the colors of the sky. He has a great sense of lighting and I love the color palette.<br /><br />Definitely going to keep going with the series.<br /><br /><a href="https://mrphilipslibrary.wordpress.com/2017/09/28/paper-girls-vol-1-by-brian-k-vaughan-and-cliff-chiang/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted in Mr. Philip's Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16646905071999296967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2362627339" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4863996989337334656">3.5 terestial ⭐⭐⭐<br/><br/>November 1, 1988….the morning of Hell. Before sunrise, the paper girls are on their bikes armed with the Cleveland Paper out for delivery. Under ordinary circumstances, these girls aren’t to be messed with. Cigarette smoking, hockey sticks at the ready and equipped with flashlights, these bad-ass girls mouth off to the rowdiest street suspects, and almost defy the law…U N T I L the discovery of some alien capsule changes their fateful morning and culminates into a clash with zom</span>
  <span id="freeText4863996989337334656" style="display:none">3.5 terestial ⭐⭐⭐<br /><br />November 1, 1988….the morning of Hell. Before sunrise, the paper girls are on their bikes armed with the Cleveland Paper out for delivery. Under ordinary circumstances, these girls aren’t to be messed with. Cigarette smoking, hockey sticks at the ready and equipped with flashlights, these bad-ass girls mouth off to the rowdiest street suspects, and almost defy the law…U N T I L the discovery of some alien capsule changes their fateful morning and culminates into a clash with zombies, dinosaur birds and other sh.. never heard off. <br /><br />Between wound eating bugs and other alienware, the girls find themselves in strange surroundings that the capsule may have created and they are thrown into the midst of a whole new timeline. <br /><br />***<br /><br />Sassy, witty, badass…what is not to like? In parts weird and creepy, it’s like Christmas crack you can’t stop until the end. And it is a cliffhanger, leading to book 2.<br /><br />I liked it. A little nostalgia there for me, as I remember my paper route when I was 12. But every now and then I need that something, something that stretches normalcy out of proportions. I recommend! 😊<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2163829920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2163829920" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2163829920?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163829920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9525567905875285340">This is even stranger than Stranger Things.<br/><br/>And definitely stranger than the Saga comic book series, from the same author shall I add. Those of you who have read that series know that the world-building is complex and the characters are many, and still, it’s easy to follow and make connections. <br/><br/>But Paper Girls is a whole other story. From what I understood, there are four girls involved in some kind of discovery that has altered the planet Earth. Adults and kids are being kidnapped—relocated?? Ki</span>
  <span id="freeText9525567905875285340" style="display:none">This is even stranger than Stranger Things.<br /><br />And definitely stranger than the Saga comic book series, from the same author shall I add. Those of you who have read that series know that the world-building is complex and the characters are many, and still, it’s easy to follow and make connections. <br /><br />But Paper Girls is a whole other story. From what I understood, there are four girls involved in some kind of discovery that has altered the planet Earth. Adults and kids are being kidnapped—relocated?? Killed??<br /><br />I was interested, because I would be interested in anything Brian K. Vaughan wrote, but I had trouble following the story.<br /><br />Fortunately, the characters also have no idea what is happening, so I didn’t feel alienated by my lack of comprehension of the storyline. I felt as though I was learning at the same pace as the characters were, so that is a plus. If you’re going to make your story complicated, at least make it so that you know as much as the people in it do. And that’s what has been done here.<br /><br />I’ll keep on reading. For now, I can say I am curious about the four heroines and the whole moving through time, but I’ll lose interest soon if the fog is not lifted.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9525567905875285340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1600096020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600096020" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600096020?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600096020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12289859768449603045">Small town America, 1988, and it’s the very early morning after Halloween. Four newspaper girls out delivering see black hooded figures skulking around the neighbourhood and discover a flying saucer in a basement. Then everyone disappears like it’s the goldurn Rapture and pterodactyls are appearing in the skies! Did someone say armour-wearing Rastafarians? And look - a flying ball of stuff that makes you relive your entire life! Makes sense to me! Wait, what’s going on again…? <br/><br/>Brian K. Vaughan r</span>
  <span id="freeText12289859768449603045" style="display:none">Small town America, 1988, and it’s the very early morning after Halloween. Four newspaper girls out delivering see black hooded figures skulking around the neighbourhood and discover a flying saucer in a basement. Then everyone disappears like it’s the goldurn Rapture and pterodactyls are appearing in the skies! Did someone say armour-wearing Rastafarians? And look - a flying ball of stuff that makes you relive your entire life! Makes sense to me! Wait, what’s going on again…? <br /><br />Brian K. Vaughan returns to his comfort zone writing a comic about sassy teens spouting clever dialogue and joining him for the ride is Cliff Chiang, fresh from his celebrated run on Wonder Woman with writer Brian Azzarello. So was Paper Girls any good? Nope! Vaughan can write convincing dialogue for young characters but places them within a nonsensical plot that’s all over the shop. <br /><br />This is a time-travel story that’s also an aliens invade story that’s also an ‘80s nostalgia trip (boy am I fucking sick of those - up yours, Ernest Cline!). Our four main characters stumble through the book not really knowing what they’re supposed to do, bemused the entire time by everything, just like the reader is! I guess it’s setup for… something… and I suppose it’s meant to be… fun? I was annoyed primarily, sleepy the rest of the time. <br /><br />Cliff Chiang’s art is good – he sure knows how to draw! - and Matt Wilson’s colours make them pages look right nice and stuff. I didn’t have a problem with the art, it was perfectly fine. Did I loves it though? Eh… <br /><br />Everything else? Bah, I didn’t care about the paper-thin story that didn’t know what it wanted to be. Vaughan’s very hit and miss with me and Paper Girls definitely falls in the miss category. Check out his new (and free!) digital series, Barrier, on his Panel Syndicate site instead - Paper Girls is toilet paper! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12289859768449603045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153688542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10333980997533833782"><b>Err...Ugh and stuff</b>?<br/><br/><b>Was this really written</b> by the same guy who created <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/146415-saga' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saga</a>? Not that I'm a deliriously hysterical Saga fan or anything (yes, that's another series I read wrong), but I kinda sorta expected more from this because of Brian Vaughan's involvement. <b>What more</b> was I expecting, you ask? Well more <b>maturity</b>, for one. Okay, so the fact that this is called Paper GIRLS as opposed to um, you know, <b>Paper WOMEN</b>, should kinda sorta have clued me in as to the <b>age of the characters</b>. But it didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText10333980997533833782" style="display:none"><b>Err...Ugh and stuff</b>?<br><br><b>Was this really written</b> by the same guy who created <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/146415-saga" rel="nofollow noopener">Saga</a>? Not that I'm a deliriously hysterical Saga fan or anything (yes, that's another series I read wrong), but I kinda sorta expected more from this because of Brian Vaughan's involvement. <b>What more</b> was I expecting, you ask? Well more <b>maturity</b>, for one. Okay, so the fact that this is called Paper GIRLS as opposed to um, you know, <b>Paper WOMEN</b>, should kinda sorta have clued me in as to the <b>age of the characters</b>. But it didn't, so it didn't. <b>A slightly clueless shrimp</b> is me and stuff. <i>Note to self: blurbs from now on you shall read, before graphic novels you shall buy.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524741702ra/25435926.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Anything else</b>? Err...No? Apart from despicably young, <b>meh characters</b>, that is. And a super <b>meh story</b>. And a super super <b>meh 80s setting</b>. And super super super <b>meh dialogues</b>. And super super super super <b>meh everything</b>. But hey, it's not <b>ALL bad and meh</b> and stuff! Oh no, it's not! And thank fish for that! It's also super super super super super <b>flat</b> and <b>unemotional</b> and <b>oh-wow-I-really-couldn't-care-less and stuff</b>! Yay and stuff! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525977658ra/25518965.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>My Moral Making Factory is Presently on Strike and So Am I Life Sucks and Stuff Crappy Non Review</b> (MMMFiPoSaSAILSaSCNR™) is: Bye now. Also: you are quite welcome, my Flimsy Decapods. <b>And stuff</b>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14082783870686109102">Eh. After calling it quits on the <i>Saga</i> series (because I realized, several volumes deep, that I simply did not care about it), I thought I'd give a different series from Vaughan a try, because my friends all seem to love his stories so much that I kept feeling like I was missing out on something. After reading this, I'm convinced that his work just isn't for me. The artwork is super fun and lively, but this volume didn't catch me at all. I <i>might</i> give the second volume a try, but it's feeling unl</span>
  <span id="freeText14082783870686109102" style="display:none">Eh. After calling it quits on the <i>Saga</i> series (because I realized, several volumes deep, that I simply did not care about it), I thought I'd give a different series from Vaughan a try, because my friends all seem to love his stories so much that I kept feeling like I was missing out on something. After reading this, I'm convinced that his work just isn't for me. The artwork is super fun and lively, but this volume didn't catch me at all. I <i>might</i> give the second volume a try, but it's feeling unlikely right now.<br /><br /><b>Content warnings</b> for severe homophobia and homophobic slurs (why is almost nobody talking about this...?)</span>

<div id="review_1583621883" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1583621883" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1583621883?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1583621883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17164192708858489370">I am in two minds about this graphic novel - I really enjoyed the story told and I see great potential for the future of this series, but at the same time the art left me mainly unimpressed.<br/><br/>This is the story of four paper girls who are on their early morning route when weird things start happening. To be perfectly honest, I don't have everything figured out just yet but the little clues scattered throughout this volume have me highly intrigued and looking forward to the next part. And that last </span>
  <span id="freeText17164192708858489370" style="display:none">I am in two minds about this graphic novel - I really enjoyed the story told and I see great potential for the future of this series, but at the same time the art left me mainly unimpressed.<br /><br />This is the story of four paper girls who are on their early morning route when weird things start happening. To be perfectly honest, I don't have everything figured out just yet but the little clues scattered throughout this volume have me highly intrigued and looking forward to the next part. And that last page? Consider me hooked.<br /><br />I loved the main characters and especially their interaction. Each one of the girls seems like a fully developed character and their reactions always made sense. I love the loyalty between those girls, even though they only just met. The nostalgia of this story set in the 80s is very well done and the setting felt real enough to have me along for the ride.<br /><br />Where this fell a bit flat for me (especially when compared to Saga) is the art. The colours are very muted and the art altogether is not very sharp. I did, however, appreciate the few panels that took up most of a page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17164192708858489370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1566688611" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566688611" />
    <a title="Chad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25388909-chad"><img alt="Chad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589745633p2/25388909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566688611?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chad" href="/user/show/25388909-chad">Chad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566688611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer414518274023680230">I loved Cliff Chiang's art and characters. The main characters are 4 paper girls who don't take crap from anyone. They all have individual personalities and likenesses. The book is set during the 80's and reminds me of E.T. or Goonies. People in town are starting to disappear and strange things start occurring. The story was somewhat confusing. I didn't know what was going on for a long while.<br/><br/><i>Received an advance copy from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8078497647154719698">I picked this up in a whim at the library today. I have seen a lot of friends of mine on Instagram reading it so I thought I’d give it a shot.<br/>SO MUCH FUN!!<br/>My only complaint is that the story is a little bit rushed, I’d like some time to let each girl get their own character development backstory or something just so it’s easier to distinguish between a few of the minor character girls. I love the story though! And set in the late 80s and the tough girl and the pop culture references, I was in gr</span>
  <span id="freeText8078497647154719698" style="display:none">I picked this up in a whim at the library today. I have seen a lot of friends of mine on Instagram reading it so I thought I’d give it a shot.<br />SO MUCH FUN!!<br />My only complaint is that the story is a little bit rushed, I’d like some time to let each girl get their own character development backstory or something just so it’s easier to distinguish between a few of the minor character girls. I love the story though! And set in the late 80s and the tough girl and the pop culture references, I was in graphic novel heaven! Not to mention the colors of the art is so appealing, each frame with different, bold neon pink, orange, purples and blues. I’ll definitely pick up the next ones!!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IBQic811bhBLv/x88EpoI3RhhUsCGl/GiuPsPo5EkR6Q3oao6X1mVcnN7sMTmBn7Wth3yu+eoAN2YfpigJQ0FQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pjw90zHydhZOzgUjQ/liVSkOpZieLeGdkmQtFHpqI2EW9pkIFfp+U8y8F5ygKxONB7dXGXOpHlhu5jtIdLqGag==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_25756608').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_25756608').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_25756608').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

      $('bookCover_44426058').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>
